RATING: 8
I love the dice, and enjoy the quirky art and humor of Quarriors! The whole package appeals to me and it just looks amazing from tin, to insert, to components (apart from the at first very crinkly dice bags - they get worn in quickly).

My initial impression of the gameplay was rather weak. It felt like a letdown of such a great premise, but having played the game some more and readjusted my expectations, I've come to really enjoy it as a great filler.

The original rules work only as a quick, random, and barely enjoyable dice-fest, but feel very lacking, not even up to filler status. However, with [b]the Advanced Capture, and Expert Culling Rules[/b] it turns into a much more tactical dice-fest that can be fully enjoyed even by gamers.

I quite like Quarriors! and it becomes much better still when combined with Quarriors! Quarmageddon. Its excellent box insert allows for super fast setup and tear down of the game, making it the true filler it should be. This will now be a steady closer on our game nights.


[b]Here are the rules we play by now:[/b]
* Advanced Capture Rule
* The Totally Expert Rule of Culling
* 3 Spells in the Wilds (normal rules, but we experimented with 4 Spells for a while)
* 7 Creatures in the Wilds (we used 8 for 15+ games, to make the Wilds be 4 rows of 4 cards with the 1 extra Spell and the Corrupted Quiddity Resource Cards). :p
* Portals are a regular Basic Resource in the Wilds (we experimented with having each player start with one instead of a Basic Quiddity and having no Portals in the Wild)
* 2-Player games are played to 20 Glory, 3 to 15 Glory, and 4 to 12 Glory as per the normal rules (we played every game to 20 Glory for 15+ games)

In short, we're back to the rules as written plus the [b]Optional Rules for Truly Epic Quarriors[/b]. :)


[i]However, we are tempted to try the house rule where an Assistant doesn't get Culled when Scoring, and instead allow you to Cull any other 1 die in its place.[/i]
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
I love that the replay value is increased by providing various cards for each type of die, so while a Death Incarnation is always a Death Incarnation, its exact efficacy can vary from game to game.  There are very interesting choices to make in this game.  The biggest downside is that players can dither with the dice on their turn, trying to min/max, but if you play with people who are willing to take chances (It [b]is[/b] a bloody dice game, after all!) just to see how it will work out, you should be just fine.  Also, gaining familiarity with the cards and game in general should help.  Otherwise, it plays nice and fast, and more importantly, I keep itching to play it again.

Don't let the MSRP scare you too badly:  You get 130 custom dice (5 of each special die, with a few extra basic [custom] dice), and several variations of each associated Power Card, as well as a nice dice bag for each player, and scoring cubes that actually match the bags' colors.  The cards are the cheap part, but they lend so, so much more replayability to the game — as if the unpredictable dice themselves didn't.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6

RATING: 8
LOTS of dice! What's not to love about it? If you like dice in your games, by all means, get this game. The "deck building" aspect of the game makes this a really different experience from others. Obviously, this game relies somewhat in luck, but you can mitigate the luck factor with good choices throughout the game. Games are relatively quick and you can't beat the satisfaction of pulling out a cool combo from the available dice.

RATING: 3
There is too much randomness in this game to recommend it to anyone but those that enjoy light games with lots of luck.

You have the first random element of "which dice am I going to draw this round" combined with the second random element of "what side are my dice going to land on?". On top of that, the dice design means that the individual dice mechanics can't be made to complex, because everything is represented through symbols. These two elements combine to make your game dull and uncontrollable, as you'll often just end up with mana rolls on all your monsters, preventing you from even attempting to get points.
